# User Engagement Analysis

- Imports
- Cleaning
- Analysis
- Recommendation
- Further Analysis

## Imports


```python
#import library
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import datetime as dt

import plotly.offline
import plotly.express as px
from plotly.subplots import make_subplots
import plotly.graph_objects as go
import plotly.figure_factory as ff


import statsmodels.api as sm
from statsmodels.stats import diagnostic as diag
from statsmodels.stats.outliers_influence import variance_inflation_factor

```


```python
#import data
df = pd.read_csv('showwcase_sessions.csv')
```

## Cleaning
- Removed rows containing NA values. Changed data types of certain columns. 
- Since **session_duration** must be longer than **inactive_duration**, we removed all rows this requirement was not met. 
- Calculate active duration, which we defined as:
> #### active_duration = session_duration - inactive_duration
- Create variable **weekend** to measure 
- Created a variable that measures user engagement called **engagement_index**, which we defined as a function of **input_index**, and **active duration**
> #### engagement_index = g(input_index, active_duration) = input_index * active_duration
> #### input_index = f(session_likes_given, session_comments_given, session_projects_given)
> Each input get the following score: like = 1 point, comment = 2 points, project = 3 points, thus
> #### input_index = 1 point * session_likes_given + 2 points * sesssion_comments_given + 3 points * session_projects_given
- Since **engagement_index** is highly skewed we log-transform it into **log_engagement**


```python
#check NA 
df.apply(lambda x: x.isnull().sum())
df = df.dropna()
df.shape

#change variables to integer
for col in ['session_id', 'customer_id']:
    df[col] = df[col].astype(int)
    
#change login_date to datetime object and rearrange dataframe by asending pattern of login_date
df['login_date'] = pd.to_datetime(df['login_date'])
df.sort_values(by = ['login_date'], inplace = True)

#create engagement_index:
#consider engagement levels projects > comment > likes.
#for now we consider projects(3 points), comment(2 points), like(1 point)
project_score = 3
comment_score = 2
like_score = 1
df['input_index'] = project_score * df['session_projects_added'] + comment_score * df['session_comments_given'] + like_score * df['session_likes_given']

#actual duration, but...
df['active_duration'] = df['session_duration'] - df['inactive_duration']

#drop all rows with wrong inactive duration
df = df[df['session_duration'] > df['inactive_duration']]

#define engagement
df['engagement_index'] = (df['input_index'] * df['active_duration'])/60

#create weekend variable
#Monday is 0 and Sunday is 6 in datetime object
df['weekend'] = df['login_date'].apply(lambda x: True if x.weekday() in [5, 6] else False)

#inactive status
def selector(row):
    if row['projects_added'] == False and row['likes_given'] == False and row['comment_given'] == False:
        return True
    else: 
        return False
df['no_action'] = df.apply(lambda x: selector(x), axis = 1)

#check if engagement distribution needs log transformation
print(stats.kurtosis(df['engagement_index'], fisher = True)) #acceptable
print(stats.skew(df['engagement_index'])) #highly skewed

#log transform engagement
df['log_engagement']  = np.log(df['engagement_index'] + 2.72)

```

    2.673377109243809
    1.5444476124456412
    

## Analysis
### 1. During Oct 2019, a total of 2259 likes, 484 comments, and 329 projects were added by 43 users. 


```python
print(len(df['customer_id'].unique()))
df_sum = df[['session_likes_given', 'session_comments_given', 'session_projects_added']].sum()
fig = go.Figure()

fig.add_trace(go.Bar(x = df_sum.index, 
                     y = df_sum,
                     text = df_sum,
                    textposition = 'auto'))
```

### 2. Of all the sessions in the record, more sessions have at least one like/comment/project than sessions without any like/comment/project. 


```python
true = [df['likes_given'].sum(), df['comment_given'].sum(), df['projects_added'].sum()]
false = [len(df) - actions[0], len(df) - actions[1], len(df) - actions[2]]
fig = go.Figure()
dict = {'True': true, 'False': false}
for i in ['True', 'False']:
    fig.add_trace(go.Bar(
    x = ['At Leat 1 Like', 'At Least 1 Comment', 'At Least 1 Project'],
    y = dict[i],
    text = dict[i],
    name = i,
    ))
fig.show()
```

var gd = document.getElementById('67109594-9051-4b8a-a779-a1d38a9e8dbb');
var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

// Listen for the removal of the full notebook cells
var notebookContainer = gd.closest('#notebook-container');
if (notebookContainer) {{
    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });
            </script>
        </div>


### 3. **Likes** is the most common type of engagement input in each session, followed by **comments**, and finally **projects**. 


```python
fig = ff.create_distplot([df['session_projects_added'], df['session_likes_given'], df['session_comments_given']], 
                        ['projects', 'likes', 'comments'], show_rug = False, bin_size = 1)
fig.show()
```

            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);

            observer.disconnect();

    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});

    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

### 4.If we look at the likes/comments/projects made by each user in October 2019, we would see the following distribution. 


```python
df_by_customer_sum = df.groupby('customer_id').sum()

fig = go.Figure()

dict = {'session_likes_given': 'total_likes', 'session_comments_given': 'total_comments', 'session_projects_added':'total_projcets'}
for i in ['session_likes_given', 'session_comments_given','session_projects_added']:
    fig.add_trace(go.Box(y = df_by_customer_sum[i], name = dict[i]))
    
fig.show()
```

var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

// Listen for the removal of the full notebook cells
var notebookContainer = gd.closest('#notebook-container');
if (notebookContainer) {{
    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });

### 5.What days of the week do these user engagement take place? On Saturdays and Sundays, the center of distribution of projects added are higher. 


```python
df['day_of_week'] = df['login_date'].apply(lambda x: x.weekday())
df['day_of_week'] = df['day_of_week'].map({0: 'Monday', 
                                           1: 'Tuesday', 
                                           2: 'Wednesday', 
                                           3: 'Thursday', 
                                           4: 'Friday', 
                                           5: 'Saturday', 
                                           6: 'Sunday'})
fig = px.box(df, x = 'day_of_week', y = 'log_engagement')
fig.show()

fig = px.box(df, x = 'day_of_week', y = 'session_projects_added')
fig.show()
```

### 6.So, when we group the sessions into weekday and weekend, the center of distribution of **log_engagement** is higher during weekend than weekday. 


```python
fig = px.histogram(df, x = 'log_engagement', color = 'weekend', marginal = 'box', nbins = 30, barmode = 'overlay')
    
fig.update_traces(opacity=0.75)
fig.show()

```

var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

// Listen for the removal of the full notebook cells
var notebookContainer = gd.closest('#notebook-container');
if (notebookContainer) {{
    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });
            </script>

var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

// Listen for the removal of the full notebook cells
var notebookContainer = gd.closest('#notebook-container');
if (notebookContainer) {{
    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });

### 7. Some users logged in much more frequently than others as shown by the distribution of user total logins.We also see there is a positive assocaition between likes/comment/projects and the number of logins. 


```python
#customers reoccurring logins
#df_by_customer = df.groupby('customer_id')['session_id'].count()
fig = px.histogram(x = df.groupby('customer_id')['session_id'].count(), nbins = 10)
fig.show()
```

var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

if (notebookContainer) {{
    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });

### 8. We can identify whether a user is a weekend user by seeing if the user's login time is disproportionately focused on weekend.


```python
df_by_customer_sum['session_count'] = df.groupby('customer_id')['session_id'].count()
df_by_customer_sum['session_count'] = df_by_customer_sum['session_count'].astype(float)
#weekend user
df_by_customer_sum['weekend_prop'] = df_by_customer_sum['weekend']/df_by_customer_sum['session_count']
df_by_customer_sum['weekend_user'] = df_by_customer_sum['weekend_prop'].apply(lambda x: True if x > 2/7 else False)

```

### 9. Interestingly, users who disproportinately prefer to log in on the weekends spend more on comments and projects, while less time on likes. 


```python
for i in ['session_likes_given', 'session_comments_given', 'session_projects_added']:
    fig = px.scatter(df_by_customer_sum, y = 'active_duration',
                     x = i,
                    marginal_x = 'box', marginal_y = 'box', 
                     color = 'weekend_user',
                     trendline = 'ols')
    fig.show()
```

var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

// Listen for the removal of the full notebook cells
var notebookContainer = gd.closest('#notebook-container');
if (notebookContainer) {{
    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });

var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

// Listen for the removal of the full notebook cells
var notebookContainer = gd.closest('#notebook-container');
if (notebookContainer) {{
    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });
            </script>

### 10. The association between **bugs_in_session** and **active_duration** or **log_engagement** is very weak.Even if we control the boolean variable whether or not a bug is in session **bug_occured**, the association is still pretty weak, with R^2 being approximately 0. 


```python
for i in ['active_duration', 'log_engagement']:
    fig = px.scatter(df, y = i,
                     x = 'bugs_in_session',
                    marginal_x = 'box', marginal_y = 'box', 
                     #color = 'weekend',
                     trendline = 'ols')
    fig.show()

fig = px.scatter(df, y = 'active_duration',
             x = 'session_likes_given',
            marginal_x = 'box', marginal_y = 'box', 
             facet_col = 'bug_occured',
             trendline = 'ols')
fig.show()
```

var gd = document.getElementById('9e4aeebc-7422-46e2-aaea-50cd3bf63598');
var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

// Listen for the removal of the full notebook cells
var notebookContainer = gd.closest('#notebook-container');
if (notebookContainer) {{
    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });
            </script>

var x = new MutationObserver(function (mutations, observer) {{
        var display = window.getComputedStyle(gd).display;
        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}
}});

// Listen for the removal of the full notebook cells
var notebookContainer = gd.closest('#notebook-container');

    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

// Listen for the clearing of the current output cell
var outputEl = gd.closest('.output');
if (outputEl) {{
    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                };

        if (!display || display === 'none') {{
            console.log([gd, 'removed!']);
            Plotly.purge(gd);
            observer.disconnect();
        }}

    x.observe(notebookContainer, {childList: true});
}}

    x.observe(outputEl, {childList: true});
}}

                        })
                };
                });

### 11. Using the cumulative sum of like, projects, and comments of individual user, we found that most users are constantly making inputs on showwcase.


```python
df['user_likes_cum'] = df.groupby(['customer_id'])['session_likes_given'].cumsum()
df['user_comments_cum'] = df.groupby(['customer_id'])['session_comments_given'].cumsum()
df['user_projects_cum'] = df.groupby(['customer_id'])['session_projects_added'].cumsum()

#histogram of total likes, posts, comments, group by user
fig = make_subplots(rows = 1, cols = 3)
row = 1
for i in ['user_likes_cum', 'user_comments_cum', 'user_projects_cum']:
    for j in list(df['customer_id'].unique()):
        df_filtered = df[df['customer_id'] == j]
        fig.add_trace(
                go.Scatter(
                    x = df_filtered['login_date'], 
                    y = df_filtered[i],
                    ),
            row = 1,
            col = row)
    row += 1
fig.show()

```

            <script type="text/javascript">
                require(["plotly"], function(Plotly) {

### 13. Linear regression models suggest that likes/comments/projects are associated with engagement and there is also interaction between session_comments_given and bug_occured


```python
from statsmodels.formula.api import ols
fit = ols('log_engagement ~ session_likes_given + session_projects_added + (session_comments_given) * C(bug_occured) + C(inactive_status)',data =df).fit()
fit.summary()
```




<table class="simpletable">
<caption>OLS Regression Results</caption>
<tr>
  <th>Dep. Variable:</th>     <td>log_engagement</td>  <th>  R-squared:         </th> <td>   0.367</td>
